- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# Task: Understand ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine Architecture

## Objective
Produce a comprehensive architecture analysis of the MergeTree storage engine, the core table engine in ClickHouse, covering its data organization, merge process, and query execution path.

## Steps
1. Find the MergeTree implementation in `src/Storages/MergeTree/`
2. Trace the write path: how INSERTs create new data parts
3. Trace the merge path: how background merges combine parts
4. Trace the read path: how SELECT queries scan parts with index skipping
5. Create `architecture_analysis.md` in `/workspace/` documenting:
   - High-level MergeTree architecture diagram (text-based)
   - Data part structure (columns, marks, primary index, skip indices)
   - Write path: from INSERT to committed part
   - Merge path: merge selection, merge algorithm, part replacement
   - Read path: part pruning, mark selection, column reading
   - Key source files with their roles
   - At least 10 specific file paths referenced

## Key Reference Files
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` — base class
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` — write path
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` — merge logic
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` — read path

## Success Criteria
- architecture_analysis.md exists
- Covers write, merge, and read paths
- References at least 10 specific source files
- Describes data part structure

     1→# ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine Architecture Analysis
     2→
     3→## Executive Summary
     4→
     5→MergeTree is the core table engine in ClickHouse, designed for highly efficient storage and querying of large volumes of structured data. It uses an append-only design where new data is written as immutable sorted parts, with background merge processes combining parts over time. The architecture is optimized for analytics workloads with column-oriented storage, sophisticated indexing, and intelligent query optimization.
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## 1. High-Level Architecture Diagram
    10→
    11→```
    12→┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    13→│                     ClickHouse MergeTree                        │
    14→└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
    15→
    16→┌─────────────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐  ┌──────────────────────┐
    17→│   INSERT Path   │  │    MERGE Path    │  │     SELECT Path      │
    18→│                 │  │                  │  │                      │
    19→│ ┌─────────────┐ │  │ ┌──────────────┐ │  │ ┌──────────────────┐ │
    20→│ │  Parser &   │ │  │ │  Merge       │ │  │ │ Query Planner    │ │
    21→│ │  Optimizer  │ │  │ │  Selector    │ │  │ │ & Optimizer      │ │
    22→│ └──────┬──────┘ │  │ └──────┬───────┘ │  │ └────────┬─────────┘ │
    23→│        │        │  │        │         │  │         │           │
    24→│ ┌──────▼──────┐ │  │ ┌──────▼──────┐ │  │ ┌───────▼──────────┐ │
    25→│ │  Data       │ │  │ │  Merge      │ │  │ │ Partition &      │ │
    26→│ │  Writer    │ │  │ │  Algorithm  │ │  │ │ Mark Pruning     │ │
    27→│ └──────┬──────┘ │  │ └──────┬──────┘ │  │ └────────┬─────────┘ │
    28→│        │        │  │        │

/// This allows efficient selection by primary key range predicate.\\n111: ///\\n112: /// Additionally:\\n113: ///\\n114: /// The date column is specified. Modes determine additional actions during merge:\\n138: /// - Ordinary - don't do anything special\\n139: /// - Collapsing - collapse pairs of rows with the opposite values of sign_columns for the same values\\n140: ///   of primary key (cf. CollapsingSortedTransform.h)\\n141: /// - Replacing - for all rows with the same primary key keep only the latest one.   "content": "# ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine Architecture Analysis\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nMergeTree is the core table engine in ClickHouse, designed for highly efficient storage and querying of large volumes of structured data. It uses an append-only design where new data is written as immutable sorted parts, with background merge processes combining parts over time. The architecture is optimized for analytics workloads with column-oriented storage, sophisticated indexing, and intelligent query optimization.\n\n---\n\n## 1. High-Level Architecture Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 2. Core Architecture Components\n\n### 2.1 MergeTreeData - Central Orchestrator\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h`\n\nMergeTreeData is the central class managing the entire storage engine:\n\n- **DataPartSet Management**: Maintains active parts with `ActiveDataPartSet` using a sorted map indexed by `MergeTreePartInfo`\n- **Metadata**: Stores table schema, partitioning expression, primary key, and index definitions\n- **Transaction Support**: Manages MVCC with transaction snapshots for consistent reads\n- **Mutex Hierarchy**: Thread-safe part management with `data_parts_mutex`\n- **Background Jobs**: Coordinates merge and mutation tasks through `BackgroundJobsAssignee`\n\n### 2.2 IMergeTreeDataPart - Part Abstraction\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`\n\nBase class for all data part implementations:\n\n- **Part Identity**: Name (e.g., `partition_0_1_5_2`), UUID, modification time\n- **Metadata**: Column list, checksums, index granularity information\n- **State Tracking**: Part state machine (PreActive \u2192 Active \u2192 Outdated \u2192 Deleting)\n- **Reader Factory**: Creates readers for specific column/mark ranges\n- **Concrete Subclasses**:\n  - `MergeTreeDataPartWide`: Wide format (one file per column) - optimal for large parts\n  - `MergeTreeDataPartCompact`: Compact format (all columns in one file) - optimal for small parts\n\n### 2.3 MergeTreePartInfo - Part Naming and Hierarchyy\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePartInfo.h`\n\nEncodes part hierarchy in its name: `partition_id_min_block_max_block_level_mutation`\n\n- **Partition ID**: Logical partition identifier (e.g., date, month)\n- **Block Range**: [min_block, max_block] identifies rows by generation number\n- **Level**: Merge depth (0=initial part, 1=merged 2 parts, 2+=merged multiple times)\n- **Mutation**: Version number if part contains mutations\n- **Containment Logic**: Method `contains()` determines if one part fully contains another based on block ranges and levels\n\n---\n\n## 3. Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### 3.1 Process Flow\n\n```\nINSERT query\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeSink (Sink.h)\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts\n    \u251c\u2500 Partition pruning by partitioning expression\n    \u251c\u2500 Group rows into blocks per partition\n    \u2514\u2500 Create BlocksWithPartition vector\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPart\n    \u251c\u2500 Generate temporary part name (tmp_...)\n    \u251c\u2500 Create part directory structure\n    \u251c\u2500 Allocate disk space reservation\n    \u2514\u2500 Build part using MergeTreeDataPartBuilder\n    \u2193\nMergedBlockOutputStream (Wide/Compact format)\n    \u251c\u2500 Write column data in blocks (granules)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Column serialization per granule\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Compression applied\n    \u251c\u2500 Write marks files (data.mrk*, *.mrk)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Track seek positions for granule boundaries\n    \u251c\u2500 Build primary index (primary.idx)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Sample primary key values at mark boundaries\n    \u2514\u2500 Build skip indices (skp_idx_*.idx)\n    \u2193\nMetadata Finalization\n    \u251c\u2500 Compute and write column checksums (checksums.txt)\n    \u251c\u2500 Write columns manifest (columns.txt)\n    \u251c\u2500 Write partition value if custom partitioning (partition.dat)\n    \u2514\u2500 Write index granularity info\n    \u2193\nCommit to Active Set\n    \u251c\u2500 Rename tmp_* \u2192 partition_min_max_0\n    \u251c\u2500 Add to ActiveDataPartSet\n    \u251c\u2500 Update transaction metadata\n    \u2514\u2500 Notify background processes of new part\n    \u2193\nTask Complete\n```\n\n### 3.2 Key Classes and Files\n\n| File Path | Role |\n|-----------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.h` | Main write orchestrator, partition splitting |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` | Write implementation, temp part creation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.h` | Column data and index writing for Wide parts |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` | Stream buffer management and compression |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.h` | INSERT sink interface connecting parser to writer |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartBuilder.h` | Part object construction with metadata |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartBuilder.cpp` | Builder implementation and part type selection |\n\n### 3.3 Data Part Structure on Disk\n\n**Wide Format (for large parts)**:\n```\npartition_0_1_5_2/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 columns.txt              # List of all columns and their types\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx              # Primary key index (compact, sampled at marks)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_name1.idx        # Skip index for index \"name1\"\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_name2.idx        # Skip index for index \"name2\"\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name1.bin         # Compressed column data\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name1.mrk3        # Marks for column_name1\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name2.bin         # Compressed column data\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name2.mrk3        # Marks for column_name2\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 checksums.txt            # File checksums for integrity verification\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 partition.dat            # Partition expression value (optional)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 count.txt               # Total row count\n\nMark file (.mrk3) contains:\n  - Compressed block offsets (8 bytes each)\n  - Uncompressed block offsets (8 bytes each)\n  - Row count in granule (4 bytes)\n  For each granule boundary\n```\n\n**Compact Format (for small parts, <10MB)**:\n```\npartition_0_1_5_2/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 columns.txt\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 data.bin                 # All columns in single file\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 data.mrk3               # Array of marks for all columns\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 checksums.txt\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 count.txt\n```\n\n### 3.4 Marks and Granularity\n\n- **Granule**: Logical unit of data (typically 8192 rows in non-adaptive mode)\n- **Mark**: Pair of offsets (compressed position in .bin file, uncompressed position in memory)\n- **Adaptive Granularity**: Adjusts granule size based on row size to maintain consistent granule sizes in bytes\n- **Mark Range**: [mark_id_start, mark_id_end] specifies which granules to read\n\n---\n\n## 4. Merge Path: Combining Parts\n\n### 4.1 Merge Selection Process\n\n```\nBackground Scheduler (MergeTreeBackgroundExecutor)\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge\n    \u251c\u2500 Step 1: Get Candidate Parts\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ActiveDataPartSet::getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n    \u2502       Filters to visible, non-locked parts\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Step 2: Determine Mergeable Ranges\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 getPossibleMergeRanges()\n    \u2502       Groups consecutive parts by partition\n    \u2502       Checks can_merge_callback for conflicts\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 Step 3: Select Optimal Parts\n        \u2514\u2500 selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            Uses merge selector strategy:\n            \u251c\u2500 Simple: Merge smallest adjacent parts\n            \u251c\u2500 TTL-based: Prioritize parts with expired TTL\n            \u251c\u2500 Balanced: Balance part count and size\n            \u2514\u2500 Graphite: Coarsen time-series data\n\nDecision: SelectPartsDecision (SELECTED | CANNOT_SELECT | NOTHING_TO_MERGE)\n```\n\n### 4.2 FutureMergedMutatedPart - Merge Task Specification\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/FutureMergedMutatedPart.h`\n\nDescribes the merge operation to perform:\n\n- **Source Parts**: `DataPartsVector parts` - ordered list of parts to merge\n- **Result Info**: `name`, `part_info` with new min/max blocks and incremented `level`\n- **Merge Type**: Regular merge vs. mutation vs. TTL cleanup\n- **Blocking Parts**: Parts that can be removed after merge completes\n\n### 4.3 Merge Execution - MergeTask\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h`\n\nExecutes the actual merge as a coroutine-like task:\n\n```\nMergeTask::execute() (called repeatedly until returns false)\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 1: Preparation\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Create output part directory structure\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Prepare readers for all input parts\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Setup merge algorithm (column-wise or block-wise)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Initialize progress tracking\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 2: Horizontal Merge (combine row sets)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Read rows from input parts in sorted order\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Apply merging logic (e.g., collapse, replace, sum)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Handle mutations if needed\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Write output blocks via MergedBlockOutputStream\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Update merge progress\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 3: Vertical Merge (rebuild indices)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Rebuild primary index from merged data\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Rebuild skip indices\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Verify data integrity with checksums\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 Stage 4: Commit Merge\n        \u251c\u2500 Finalize output part (checksums, columns.txt)\n        \u251c\u2500 Rename from tmp_* to final name\n        \u251c\u2500 Add to ActiveDataPartSet\n        \u251c\u2500 Remove source parts\n        \u2514\u2500 Clean up temporary files\n```\n\n### 4.4 Merge Modes (MergeTreeData::MergingParams)\n\n| Mode | Behavior |\n|------|----------|\n| **Ordinary** | Simple concatenation and re-sorting |\n| **Replacing** | Keep only latest row per primary key (by version or insert order) |\n| **Collapsing** | Remove pairs of rows with opposite `sign` column values |\n| **Summing** | Sum numeric non-key columns for each primary key |\n| **Aggregating** | Merge pre-computed aggregate states |\n| **Graphite** | Coarsen time-series data for monitoring systems |\n\n### 4.5 Key Classes and Files\n\n| File Path | Role |\n|-----------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.h` | Merge selection logic and heuristics |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` | Implementation of merge selector |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h` | Core merge execution task (coroutine-like) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` | Merge algorithm stages: horizontal, vertical, commit |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeList.h` | Merge progress tracking and monitoring |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/ActiveDataPartSet.h` | Maintains set of active parts with containment logic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/ActiveDataPartSet.cpp` | Part set operations and deduplication |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Read Path: SELECT Query Execution\n\n### 5.1 Query Planning and Optimization\n\n```\nSELECT query\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n    \u251c\u2500 Create ReadFromMergeTree processor\n    \u251c\u2500 Select parts covering requested range\n    \u2514\u2500 Return QueryPlan with optimized execution\n    \u2193\nPart Pruning (Partition Elimination)\n    \u251c\u2500 Use partition expressions to eliminate partitions\n    \u251c\u2500 PartitionPruner evaluates where conditions\n    \u2514\u2500 Keep only matching partitions\n    \u2193\nPrimary Key Index Filtering\n    \u251c\u2500 Convert WHERE clause to KeyCondition\n    \u251c\u2500 KeyCondition::checkInRange() on part min/max values\n    \u2514\u2500 Determine mark ranges to read per part\n    \u2193\nSkip Index Filtering (Secondary Indices)\n    \u251c\u2500 Evaluate index conditions per granule\n    \u251c\u2500 Uses IMergeTreeIndexCondition\n    \u251c\u2500 Types: minmax, bloom filter, set, full-text, etc.\n    \u2514\u2500 Further refine mark ranges\n    \u2193\nMark Range Selection\n    \u251c\u2500 Merge adjacent/overlapping mark ranges\n    \u251c\u2500 Determine which granules to actually read\n    \u2514\u2500 Pass to reader for column retrieval\n```\n\n### 5.2 MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.h`\n\nMain query executor:\n\n- **Part Selection**: `read()` chooses which parts to scan based on constraints\n- **Index Application**: `markRangesFromPKRange()` converts primary key condition to granule ranges\n- **Multi-strategy**: Supports parallel reading, in-order reading, and parallel replicas\n- **Analysis Methods**: `estimateNumMarksToRead()` for cost estimation and projection selection\n\n### 5.3 KeyCondition - Primary Key Index\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h`\n\nEvaluates WHERE conditions against primary key ranges:\n\n- **RPN Compilation**: Converts condition DAG to Reverse Polish Notation\n- **Range Checking**: `checkInRange()` evaluates feasibility over [left_key, right_key] ranges\n- **Mask Result**: Returns `BoolMask` with (can_be_true, can_be_false) components\n- **Optimization**: Short-circuit evaluation when condition is always true/false\n- **Limitation**: Only uses prefix of primary key that can short-circuit the condition\n\n### 5.4 Skip Indices - Secondary Index Selection\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndices.h`\n\nPluggable secondary indices for further granule filtering:\n\n| Index Type | Purpose | Overhead |\n|-----------|---------|----------|\n| **minmax** | Track min/max per granule | Minimal (always built) |\n| **bloom_filter** | Fast membership testing | Medium (3-4% space) |\n| **set** | Enumerate allowed values | Low (hash set) |\n| **full-text** | Full-text search in text columns | High (inverted index) |\n| **similarity** | Vector similarity search | Very high (graph index) |\n\nIndex granule = one granule of data with one index entry\n\n### 5.5 Reader Interface - Column Data Retrieval\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeReader.h`\n\nAbstract reader interface:\n\n```cpp\nreadRows(size_t from_mark, size_t current_task_last_mark,\n         bool continue_reading, size_t max_rows_to_read,\n         Columns & res_columns)\n  \u251c\u2500 from_mark: starting granule ID\n  \u251c\u2500 current_task_last_mark: prefetch boundary for async reads\n  \u251c\u2500 continue_reading: resume from last position or seek\n  \u2514\u2500 max_rows_to_read: limit rows returned\n```\n\nConcrete implementations:\n- **MergeTreeReaderWide**: Reads Wide format (one file per column)\n- **MergeTreeReaderCompact**: Reads Compact format (all columns in one file)\n\n### 5.6 MergeTreeReaderWide - Wide Format Reading\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderWide.h`\n\nOptimized reader for Wide parts:\n\n- **Per-Column Streams**: One `MergeTreeReaderStream` per column\n- **Parallel Column Loading**: Load multiple columns concurrently\n- **Mark Caching**: Cache decompressed mark ranges in memory\n- **Prefetching**: Async prefetch upcoming granules for remote storage\n\nReading process:\n```\nreadRows()\n  \u251c\u2500 Seek each column's stream to from_mark\n  \u251c\u2500 Deserialize column data for max_rows_to_read rows\n  \u251c\u2500 Apply alter conversions if schema changed\n  \u251c\u2500 Fill missing columns with defaults\n  \u2514\u2500 Return Columns vector\n```\n\n### 5.7 Data Access Hierarchy\n\n```\nColumn Data on Disk (.bin file)\n  \u251c\u2500 Compression wrapper (e.g., LZ4, ZSTD)\n  \u251c\u2500 Serialized blocks (per granule)\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Block header (sizes, counts)\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Serialized values\n  \u2514\u2500 Footer (checksums)\n\nMark File (.mrk3) - Index into .bin\n  \u251c\u2500 Entry 0: offset to granule 0\n  \u251c\u2500 Entry 1: offset to granule 1\n  \u2514\u2500 Entry n: offset to granule n\n\nRead Process:\n  1. Load mark file into MarkCache\n  2. Seek to offset for from_mark\n  3. Stream decompression buffer\n  4. Deserialize rows until max_rows_to_read\n```\n\n### 5.8 Key Classes and Files\n\n| File Path | Role |\n|-----------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.h` | Query planning and part selection |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` | Index filtering and mark range calculation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h` | Primary key condition evaluation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp` | RPN compilation and range checking |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeReader.h` | Reader interface abstraction |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderWide.h` | Wide format reader implementation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderWide.cpp` | Column-by-column reading logic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderStream.h` | Single column read buffer with mark caching |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndices.h` | Skip index interface and implementations |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.h` | Partition elimination based on expressions |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Concurrency and Transaction Support\n\n### 6.1 Part State Machine\n\n```\nPart Lifecycle:\n\n  1. Temporary (tmp_*)\n     \u251c\u2500 Being written by MergeTreeDataWriter\n     \u2514\u2500 Not visible to queries\n\n  2. PreActive\n     \u251c\u2500 Part directory renamed to final name\n     \u251c\u2500 But not yet in ActiveDataPartSet\n     \u2514\u2500 Mutation processing in progress\n\n  3. Active\n     \u251c\u2500 In ActiveDataPartSet\n     \u251c\u2500 Visible to all new queries\n     \u2514\u2500 Can be merged with other parts\n\n  4. Outdated\n     \u251c\u2500 Covered by another part (contains() returns true)\n     \u251c\u2500 Still visible to existing transactions\n     \u2514\u2500 Can be safely deleted after transaction cleanup\n\n  5. Deleting\n     \u251c\u2500 Removal in progress\n     \u2514\u2500 Clean up directory\n```\n\n### 6.2 Transaction Snapshot Isolation\n\n- **MVCC**: Transactions see consistent snapshot of parts at snapshot time\n- **Snapshot Creation**: Records active parts set at query start\n- **Part Visibility**: Part visible if created before transaction snapshot time\n- **Outdated Part Retention**: Parts kept until all transactions using them complete\n\n### 6.3 Thread Safety\n\n- **data_parts_mutex**: RWLock protecting ActiveDataPartSet modifications\n- **DataPartsLock**: Scoped lock wrapper with timing instrumentation\n- **Atomic Operations**: Part state transitions use atomics\n- **No Copy-on-Write**: Parts are immutable once active\n\n---\n\n## 7. File Reference Summary\n\n### Core Infrastructure (10+ files referenced)\n\n1. **MergeTreeData.h** - Central orchestrator, part set management, metadata storage\n2. **IMergeTreeDataPart.h** - Abstract base class for all data parts\n3. **MergeTreePartInfo.h** - Part naming, hierarchical containment logic\n4. **MergeTreeDataWriter.h** - INSERT path, partition splitting, temp part creation\n5. **MergedBlockOutputStream.h** - Column serialization, index building, compression\n6. **MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.h** - Merge selection, part picking heuristics\n7. **MergeTask.h** - Core merge execution, horizontal/vertical stages\n8. **MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.h** - Query planning, part/mark selection\n9. **KeyCondition.h** - Primary key index evaluation, RPN condition\n10. **IMergeTreeReader.h** - Reader abstraction for column data retrieval\n11. **MergeTreeReaderWide.h** - Wide format reader with per-column streams\n12. **MergeTreeIndices.h** - Skip index interface and implementations\n13. **FutureMergedMutatedPart.h** - Merge specification and part naming\n14. **ActiveDataPartSet.h** - Active parts set with containment tracking\n15. **MergeList.h** - Merge progress monitoring and statistics\n\n### Supporting Components\n\n- **MergeTreeDataPartBuilder.h** - Part construction with metadata\n- **MergeTreeDataPartWide.h** - Wide format part implementation\n- **MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h** - Compact format part implementation\n- **MergeTreeReaderCompact.h** - Compact format reader\n- **MergeTreeReaderStream.h** - Single column read buffer with marks\n- **MergeTreeIOSettings.h** - Read/write buffer settings\n- **PartitionPruner.h** - Partition elimination\n- **RangesInDataPart.h** - Mark range management\n\n---\n\n## 8. Optimization Techniques\n\n### 8.1 Sparse Indexing\n- **Primary Key Index**: Stores only ~1/granule_size samples\n- **Storage**: Compressed in `primary.idx` file (~KB for large parts)\n- **Efficacy**: Can eliminate 90%+ of data before reading\n\n### 8.2 Adaptive Granularity\n- **Goal**: Keep granule sizes consistent despite variable row sizes\n- **Implementation**: `MergeTreeIndexGranularityAdaptive`\n- **Benefit**: Predictable I/O patterns, better parallelism\n\n### 8.3 Mark Caching\n- **Component**: `MarkCache` in-memory cache\n- **Content**: Decompressed mark ranges\n- **Hit Rate**: High for repeated scans of same columns\n- **Size Control**: Configurable via `mark_cache_size_ratio`\n\n### 8.4 Parallel Column Reading\n- **Wide Format**: Each column can read independently\n- **Threads**: Configurable thread pool for parallel reads\n- **Scheduling**: Dynamic task scheduling based on part size\n\n### 8.5 Projection Materialization\n- **Concept**: Pre-computed tables with different key structure\n- **Usage**: Automatic selection when projection query is subset of main table query\n- **Merge**: Built automatically during main part merges\n\n---\n\n## 9. Performance Characteristics\n\n### Write Performance\n- **Sequential**: Parts written sequentially to disk with compression\n- **Throughput**: Limited by compression speed and disk I/O\n- **Latency**: Sorting + compression + index building (typically 100ms-10s depending on size)\n\n### Merge Performance\n- **Throughput**: Merges are I/O bound, parallelism from multiple merges\n- **CPU Efficiency**: Merge algorithm is cache-friendly (sequential scan)\n- **Space**: Requires 2x source size temporarily for merge output\n- **Impact**: Background merges should not block inserts (async execution)\n\n### Query Performance\n- **Partition Pruning**: O(1) hash lookup of partitions\n- **Index Range Finding**: O(log n) binary search in primary key\n- **Skip Index Filtering**: O(num_granules) evaluation\n- **Column Reading**: Proportional to marks selected, parallelized\n\n---\n\n## 10. Edge Cases and Special Handling\n\n### 10.1 Mutation Processing\n- **Lazy Application**: Mutations create entries but don't modify parts immediately\n- **Query Application**: Readers apply mutations on-the-fly from mutation log\n- **Background Application**: Merge task creates new part with mutations applied\n- **Versioning**: Each part knows which mutations it contains\n\n### 10.2 TTL (Time-to-Live)\n- **TTL Index**: Tracks min/max TTL expression value per granule\n- **Cleanup**: Removes expired rows during merges\n- **Group By TTL**: Merge selector can prioritize parts with expired data\n\n### 10.3 Replicated MergeTree\n- **ZooKeeper**: Coordination of merges across replicas\n- **Merge Log**: Entries in ZooKeeper ensure consistent merge ordering\n- **Leader Election**: First replica to claim merge executes it\n- **Data Exchange**: Other replicas can fetch merged part directly\n\n### 10.4 Compact Format Selection\n- **Threshold 1**: `min_bytes_for_wide_part` (default 10MB)\n- **Threshold 2**: `min_rows_for_wide_part` (default 1M rows)\n- **Decision**: Use compact if both size AND row count below thresholds\n- **Conversion**: Automatic during merge if size grows\n\n---\n\n## 11. Key Design Insights\n\n1. **Immutability**: Parts never change once committed, enabling simple concurrency\n2. **Append-Only**: Inserts create new parts, no in-place updates or deletes\n3. **Lazy Merging**: Merges happen asynchronously in background with priority queue\n4. **Sparse Indexing**: Primary key index is ~0.1-1% of data size but can eliminate 90%+ of scans\n5. **Format Flexibility**: Wide format for analytical queries, compact format for write efficiency\n6. **Projection Materialization**: Pre-compute alternative indices automatically\n7. **Coroutine Merges**: Merges implemented as suspendable tasks, not blocking threads\n8. **MVCC Visibility**: Transactions see consistent part set snapshot independent of concurrent changes\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe MergeTree storage engine combines several key innovations:\n- **Columnar + Sorted**: Column-oriented storage with sorted primary key enables both compression and efficient range queries\n- **Hierarchical Merging**: Background merges consolidate small parts into larger ones, balancing write latency and merge cost\n- **Sparse + Layered Indexing**: Multi-level indices (primary key + skip indices) prune data efficiently\n- **Immutable Architecture**: Append-only design eliminates locking complexity and enables simple MVCC\n\nThis architecture makes ClickHouse exceptionally fast for analytical workloads with high insert throughput and complex ad-hoc queries over billions of rows.\n",

It uses an append-only design where new data is written as immutable sorted parts, with background merge processes combining parts over time. The architecture is optimized for analytics workloads with column-oriented storage, sophisticated indexing, and intelligent query optimization.\n\n---\n\n## 1. \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Core Architecture Components\n\n### 2.1 MergeTreeData - Central Orchestrator\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h`\n\nMergeTreeData is the central class managing the entire storage engine:\n\n- **DataPartSet Management**: Maintains active parts with `ActiveDataPartSet` using a sorted map indexed by `MergeTreePartInfo`\n- **Metadata**: Stores table schema, partitioning expression, primary key, and index definitions\n- **Transaction Support**: Manages MVCC with transaction snapshots for consistent reads\n- **Mutex Hierarchy**: Thread-safe part management with `data_parts_mutex`\n- **Background Jobs**: Coordinates merge and mutation tasks through `BackgroundJobsAssignee`\n\n### 2.2 IMergeTreeDataPart - Part Abstraction\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`\n\nBase class for all data part implementations:\n\n- **Part Identity**: Name (e.g., `partition_0_1_5_2`), UUID, modification time\n- **Metadata**: Column list, checksums, index granularity information\n- **State Tracking**: Part state machine (PreActive \u2192 Active \u2192 Outdated \u2192 Deleting)\n- **Reader Factory**: Creates readers for specific column/mark ranges\n- **Concrete Subclasses**:\n  - `MergeTreeDataPartWide`: Wide format (one file per column) - optimal for large parts\n  - `MergeTreeDataPartCompact`: Compact format (all columns in one file) - optimal for small parts\n\n### 2.3 MergeTreePartInfo - Part Naming and Hierarchyy\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePartInfo.h`\n\nEncodes part hierarchy in its name: `partition_id_min_block_max_block_level_mutation`\n\n- **Partition ID**: Logical partition identifier (e.g., date, month)\n- **Block Range**: [min_block, max_block] identifies rows by generation number\n- **Level**: Merge depth (0=initial part, 1=merged 2 parts, 2+=merged multiple times)\n- **Mutation**: Version number if part contains mutations\n- **Containment Logic**: Method `contains()` determines if one part fully contains another based on block ranges and levels\n\n---\n\n## 3. Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### 3.1 Process Flow\n\n```\nINSERT query\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeSink (Sink.h)\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts\n    \u251c\u2500 Partition pruning by partitioning expression\n    \u251c\u2500 Group rows into blocks per partition\n    \u2514\u2500 Create BlocksWithPartition vector\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPart\n    \u251c\u2500 Generate temporary part name (tmp_...)\n    \u251c\u2500 Create part directory structure\n    \u251c\u2500 Allocate disk space reservation\n    \u2514\u2500 Build part using MergeTreeDataPartBuilder\n    \u2193\nMergedBlockOutputStream (Wide/Compact format)\n    \u251c\u2500 Write column data in blocks (granules)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Column serialization per granule\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Compression applied\n    \u251c\u2500 Write marks files (data.mrk*, *.mrk)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Track seek positions for granule boundaries\n    \u251c\u2500 Build primary index (primary.idx)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Sample primary key values at mark boundaries\n    \u2514\u2500 Build skip indices (skp_idx_*.idx)\n    \u2193\nMetadata Finalization\n    \u251c\u2500 Compute and write column checksums (checksums.txt)\n    \u251c\u2500 Write columns manifest (columns.txt)\n    \u251c\u2500 Write partition value if custom partitioning (partition.dat)\n    \u2514\u2500 Write index granularity info\n    \u2193\nCommit to Active Set\n    \u251c\u2500 Rename tmp_* \u2192 partition_min_max_0\n    \u251c\u2500 Add to ActiveDataPartSet\n    \u251c\u2500 Update transaction metadata\n    \u2514\u2500 Notify background processes of new part\n    \u2193\nTask Complete\n```\n\n### 3.2 Key Classes and Files\n\n| File Path | Role |\n|-----------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.h` | Main write orchestrator, partition splitting |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` | Write implementation, temp part creation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.h` | Column data and index writing for Wide parts |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` | Stream buffer management and compression |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.h` | INSERT sink interface connecting parser to writer |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartBuilder.h` | Part object construction with metadata |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartBuilder.cpp` | Builder implementation and part type selection |\n\n### 3.3 Data Part Structure on Disk\n\n**Wide Format (for large parts)**:\n```\npartition_0_1_5_2/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 columns.txt              # List of all columns and their types\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx              # Primary key index (compact, sampled at marks)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_name1.idx        # Skip index for index \"name1\"\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_name2.idx        # Skip index for index \"name2\"\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name1.bin         # Compressed column data\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name1.mrk3        # Marks for column_name1\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name2.bin         # Compressed column data\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 column_name2.mrk3        # Marks for column_name2\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 checksums.txt            # File checksums for integrity verification\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 partition.dat            # Partition expression value (optional)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 count.txt               # Total row count\n\nMark file (.mrk3) contains:\n  - Compressed block offsets (8 bytes each)\n  - Uncompressed block offsets (8 bytes each)\n  - Row count in granule (4 bytes)\n  For each granule boundary\n```\n\n**Compact Format (for small parts, <10MB)**:\n```\npartition_0_1_5_2/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 columns.txt\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 data.bin                 # All columns in single file\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 data.mrk3               # Array of marks for all columns\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 checksums.txt\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 count.txt\n```\n\n### 3.4 Marks and Granularity\n\n- **Granule**: Logical unit of data (typically 8192 rows in non-adaptive mode)\n- **Mark**: Pair of offsets (compressed position in .bin file, uncompressed position in memory)\n- **Adaptive Granularity**: Adjusts granule size based on row size to maintain consistent granule sizes in bytes\n- **Mark Range**: [mark_id_start, mark_id_end] specifies which granules to read\n\n---\n\n## 4. Merge Path: Combining Parts\n\n### 4.1 Merge Selection Process\n\n```\nBackground Scheduler (MergeTreeBackgroundExecutor)\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge\n    \u251c\u2500 Step 1: Get Candidate Parts\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ActiveDataPartSet::getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n    \u2502       Filters to visible, non-locked parts\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Step 2: Determine Mergeable Ranges\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 getPossibleMergeRanges()\n    \u2502       Groups consecutive parts by partition\n    \u2502       Checks can_merge_callback for conflicts\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 Step 3: Select Optimal Parts\n        \u2514\u2500 selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            Uses merge selector strategy:\n            \u251c\u2500 Simple: Merge smallest adjacent parts\n            \u251c\u2500 TTL-based: Prioritize parts with expired TTL\n            \u251c\u2500 Balanced: Balance part count and size\n            \u2514\u2500 Graphite: Coarsen time-series data\n\nDecision: SelectPartsDecision (SELECTED | CANNOT_SELECT | NOTHING_TO_MERGE)\n```\n\n### 4.2 FutureMergedMutatedPart - Merge Task Specification\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/FutureMergedMutatedPart.h`\n\nDescribes the merge operation to perform:\n\n- **Source Parts**: `DataPartsVector parts` - ordered list of parts to merge\n- **Result Info**: `name`, `part_info` with new min/max blocks and incremented `level`\n- **Merge Type**: Regular merge vs. mutation vs. TTL cleanup\n- **Blocking Parts**: Parts that can be removed after merge completes\n\n### 4.3 Merge Execution - MergeTask\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h`\n\nExecutes the actual merge as a coroutine-like task:\n\n```\nMergeTask::execute() (called repeatedly until returns false)\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 1: Preparation\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Create output part directory structure\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Prepare readers for all input parts\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Setup merge algorithm (column-wise or block-wise)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Initialize progress tracking\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 2: Horizontal Merge (combine row sets)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Read rows from input parts in sorted order\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Apply merging logic (e.g., collapse, replace, sum)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Handle mutations if needed\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Write output blocks via MergedBlockOutputStream\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Update merge progress\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 3: Vertical Merge (rebuild indices)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Rebuild primary index from merged data\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Rebuild skip indices\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Verify data integrity with checksums\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 Stage 4: Commit Merge\n        \u251c\u2500 Finalize output part (checksums, columns.txt)\n        \u251c\u2500 Rename from tmp_* to final name\n        \u251c\u2500 Add to ActiveDataPartSet\n        \u251c\u2500 Remove source parts\n        \u2514\u2500 Clean up temporary files\n```\n\n### 4.4 Merge Modes (MergeTreeData::MergingParams)\n\n| Mode | Behavior |\n|------|----------|\n| **Ordinary** | Simple concatenation and re-sorting |\n| **Replacing** | Keep only latest row per primary key (by version or insert order) |\n| **Collapsing** | Remove pairs of rows with opposite `sign` column values |\n| **Summing** | Sum numeric non-key columns for each primary key |\n| **Aggregating** | Merge pre-computed aggregate states |\n| **Graphite** | Coarsen time-series data for monitoring systems |\n\n### 4.5 Key Classes and Files\n\n| File Path | Role |\n|-----------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.h` | Merge selection logic and heuristics |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` | Implementation of merge selector |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h` | Core merge execution task (coroutine-like) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` | Merge algorithm stages: horizontal, vertical, commit |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeList.h` | Merge progress tracking and monitoring |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/ActiveDataPartSet.h` | Maintains set of active parts with containment logic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/ActiveDataPartSet.cpp` | Part set operations and deduplication |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Read Path: SELECT Query Execution\n\n### 5.1 Query Planning and Optimization\n\n```\nSELECT query\n    \u2193\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n    \u251c\u2500 Create ReadFromMergeTree processor\n    \u251c\u2500 Select parts covering requested range\n    \u2514\u2500 Return QueryPlan with optimized execution\n    \u2193\nPart Pruning (Partition Elimination)\n    \u251c\u2500 Use partition expressions to eliminate partitions\n    \u251c\u2500 PartitionPruner evaluates where conditions\n    \u2514\u2500 Keep only matching partitions\n    \u2193\nPrimary Key Index Filtering\n    \u251c\u2500 Convert WHERE clause to KeyCondition\n    \u251c\u2500 KeyCondition::checkInRange() on part min/max values\n    \u2514\u2500 Determine mark ranges to read per part\n    \u2193\nSkip Index Filtering (Secondary Indices)\n    \u251c\u2500 Evaluate index conditions per granule\n    \u251c\u2500 Uses IMergeTreeIndexCondition\n    \u251c\u2500 Types: minmax, bloom filter, set, full-text, etc.\n    \u2514\u2500 Further refine mark ranges\n    \u2193\nMark Range Selection\n    \u251c\u2500 Merge adjacent/overlapping mark ranges\n    \u251c\u2500 Determine which granules to actually read\n    \u2514\u2500 Pass to reader for column retrieval\n```\n\n### 5.2 MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.h`\n\nMain query executor:\n\n- **Part Selection**: `read()` chooses which parts to scan based on constraints\n- **Index Application**: `markRangesFromPKRange()` converts primary key condition to granule ranges\n- **Multi-strategy**: Supports parallel reading, in-order reading, and parallel replicas\n- **Analysis Methods**: `estimateNumMarksToRead()` for cost estimation and projection selection\n\n### 5.3 KeyCondition - Primary Key Index\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h`\n\nEvaluates WHERE conditions against primary key ranges:\n\n- **RPN Compilation**: Converts condition DAG to Reverse Polish Notation\n- **Range Checking**: `checkInRange()` evaluates feasibility over [left_key, right_key] ranges\n- **Mask Result**: Returns `BoolMask` with (can_be_true, can_be_false) components\n- **Optimization**: Short-circuit evaluation when condition is always true/false\n- **Limitation**: Only uses prefix of primary key that can short-circuit the condition\n\n### 5.4 Skip Indices - Secondary Index Selection\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndices.h`\n\nPluggable secondary indices for further granule filtering:\n\n| Index Type | Purpose | Overhead |\n|-----------|---------|----------|\n| **minmax** | Track min/max per granule | Minimal (always built) |\n| **bloom_filter** | Fast membership testing | Medium (3-4% space) |\n| **set** | Enumerate allowed values | Low (hash set) |\n| **full-text** | Full-text search in text columns | High (inverted index) |\n| **similarity** | Vector similarity search | Very high (graph index) |\n\nIndex granule = one granule of data with one index entry\n\n### 5.5 Reader Interface - Column Data Retrieval\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeReader.h`\n\nAbstract reader interface:\n\n```cpp\nreadRows(size_t from_mark, size_t current_task_last_mark,\n         bool continue_reading, size_t max_rows_to_read,\n         Columns & res_columns)\n  \u251c\u2500 from_mark: starting granule ID\n  \u251c\u2500 current_task_last_mark: prefetch boundary for async reads\n  \u251c\u2500 continue_reading: resume from last position or seek\n  \u2514\u2500 max_rows_to_read: limit rows returned\n```\n\nConcrete implementations:\n- **MergeTreeReaderWide**: Reads Wide format (one file per column)\n- **MergeTreeReaderCompact**: Reads Compact format (all columns in one file)\n\n### 5.6 MergeTreeReaderWide - Wide Format Reading\n**File**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderWide.h`\n\nOptimized reader for Wide parts:\n\n- **Per-Column Streams**: One `MergeTreeReaderStream` per column\n- **Parallel Column Loading**: Load multiple columns concurrently\n- **Mark Caching**: Cache decompressed mark ranges in memory\n- **Prefetching**: Async prefetch upcoming granules for remote storage\n\nReading process:\n```\nreadRows()\n  \u251c\u2500 Seek each column's stream to from_mark\n  \u251c\u2500 Deserialize column data for max_rows_to_read rows\n  \u251c\u2500 Apply alter conversions if schema changed\n  \u251c\u2500 Fill missing columns with defaults\n  \u2514\u2500 Return Columns vector\n```\n\n### 5.7 Data Access Hierarchy\n\n```\nColumn Data on Disk (.bin file)\n  \u251c\u2500 Compression wrapper (e.g., LZ4, ZSTD)\n  \u251c\u2500 Serialized blocks (per granule)\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Block header (sizes, counts)\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Serialized values\n  \u2514\u2500 Footer (checksums)\n\nMark File (.mrk3) - Index into .bin\n  \u251c\u2500 Entry 0: offset to granule 0\n  \u251c\u2500 Entry 1: offset to granule 1\n  \u2514\u2500 Entry n: offset to granule n\n\nRead Process:\n  1. Load mark file into MarkCache\n  2. Seek to offset for from_mark\n  3. Stream decompression buffer\n  4. Deserialize rows until max_rows_to_read\n```\n\n### 5.8 Key Classes and Files\n\n| File Path | Role |\n|-----------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.h` | Query planning and part selection |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` | Index filtering and mark range calculation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h` | Primary key condition evaluation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp` | RPN compilation and range checking |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeReader.h` | Reader interface abstraction |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderWide.h` | Wide format reader implementation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderWide.cpp` | Column-by-column reading logic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReaderStream.h` | Single column read buffer with mark caching |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndices.h` | Skip index interface and implementations |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.h` | Partition elimination based on expressions |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Concurrency and Transaction Support\n\n### 6.1 Part State Machine\n\n```\nPart Lifecycle:\n\n  1. Temporary (tmp_*)\n     \u251c\u2500 Being written by MergeTreeDataWriter\n     \u2514\u2500 Not visible to queries\n\n  2. PreActive\n     \u251c\u2500 Part directory renamed to final name\n     \u251c\u2500 But not yet in ActiveDataPartSet\n     \u2514\u2500 Mutation processing in progress\n\n  3. Active\n     \u251c\u2500 In ActiveDataPartSet\n     \u251c\u2500 Visible to all new queries\n     \u2514\u2500 Can be merged with other parts\n\n  4. Outdated\n     \u251c\u2500 Covered by another part (contains() returns true)\n     \u251c\u2500 Still visible to existing transactions\n     \u2514\u2500 Can be safely deleted after transaction cleanup\n\n  5. Deleting\n     \u251c\u2500 Removal in progress\n     \u2514\u2500 Clean up directory\n```\n\n### 6.2 Transaction Snapshot Isolation\n\n- **MVCC**: Transactions see consistent snapshot of parts at snapshot time\n- **Snapshot Creation**: Records active parts set at query start\n- **Part Visibility**: Part visible if created before transaction snapshot time\n- **Outdated Part Retention**: Parts kept until all transactions using them complete\n\n### 6.3 Thread Safety\n\n- **data_parts_mutex**: RWLock protecting ActiveDataPartSet modifications\n- **DataPartsLock**: Scoped lock wrapper with timing instrumentation\n- **Atomic Operations**: Part state transitions use atomics\n- **No Copy-on-Write**: Parts are immutable once active\n\n---\n\n## 7. File Reference Summary\n\n### Core Infrastructure (10+ files referenced)\n\n1. **MergeTreeData.h** - Central orchestrator, part set management, metadata storage\n2. **IMergeTreeDataPart.h** - Abstract base class for all data parts\n3. **MergeTreePartInfo.h** - Part naming, hierarchical containment logic\n4. **MergeTreeDataWriter.h** - INSERT path, partition splitting, temp part creation\n5. **MergedBlockOutputStream.h** - Column serialization, index building, compression\n6. **MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.h** - Merge selection, part picking heuristics\n7. **MergeTask.h** - Core merge execution, horizontal/vertical stages\n8. **MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.h** - Query planning, part/mark selection\n9. **KeyCondition.h** - Primary key index evaluation, RPN condition\n10. **IMergeTreeReader.h** - Reader abstraction for column data retrieval\n11. **MergeTreeReaderWide.h** - Wide format reader with per-column streams\n12. **MergeTreeIndices.h** - Skip index interface and implementations\n13. **FutureMergedMutatedPart.h** - Merge specification and part naming\n14. **ActiveDataPartSet.h** - Active parts set with containment tracking\n15. **MergeList.h** - Merge progress monitoring and statistics\n\n### Supporting Components\n\n- **MergeTreeDataPartBuilder.h** - Part construction with metadata\n- **MergeTreeDataPartWide.h** - Wide format part implementation\n- **MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h** - Compact format part implementation\n- **MergeTreeReaderCompact.h** - Compact format reader\n- **MergeTreeReaderStream.h** - Single column read buffer with marks\n- **MergeTreeIOSettings.h** - Read/write buffer settings\n- **PartitionPruner.h** - Partition elimination\n- **RangesInDataPart.h** - Mark range management\n\n---\n\n## 8. Optimization Techniques\n\n### 8.1 Sparse Indexing\n- **Primary Key Index**: Stores only ~1/granule_size samples\n- **Storage**: Compressed in `primary.idx` file (~KB for large parts)\n- **Efficacy**: Can eliminate 90%+ of data before reading\n\n### 8.2 Adaptive Granularity\n- **Goal**: Keep granule sizes consistent despite variable row sizes\n- **Implementation**: `MergeTreeIndexGranularityAdaptive`\n- **Benefit**: Predictable I/O patterns, better parallelism\n\n### 8.3 Mark Caching\n- **Component**: `MarkCache` in-memory cache\n- **Content**: Decompressed mark ranges\n- **Hit Rate**: High for repeated scans of same columns\n- **Size Control**: Configurable via `mark_cache_size_ratio`\n\n### 8.4 Parallel Column Reading\n- **Wide Format**: Each column can read independently\n- **Threads**: Configurable thread pool for parallel reads\n- **Scheduling**: Dynamic task scheduling based on part size\n\n### 8.5 Projection Materialization\n- **Concept**: Pre-computed tables with different key structure\n- **Usage**: Automatic selection when projection query is subset of main table query\n- **Merge**: Built automatically during main part merges\n\n---\n\n## 9. Performance Characteristics\n\n### Write Performance\n- **Sequential**: Parts written sequentially to disk with compression\n- **Throughput**: Limited by compression speed and disk I/O\n- **Latency**: Sorting + compression + index building (typically 100ms-10s depending on size)\n\n### Merge Performance\n- **Throughput**: Merges are I/O bound, parallelism from multiple merges\n- **CPU Efficiency**: Merge algorithm is cache-friendly (sequential scan)\n- **Space**: Requires 2x source size temporarily for merge output\n- **Impact**: Background merges should not block inserts (async execution)\n\n### Query Performance\n- **Partition Pruning**: O(1) hash lookup of partitions\n- **Index Range Finding**: O(log n) binary search in primary key\n- **Skip Index Filtering**: O(num_granules) evaluation\n- **Column Reading**: Proportional to marks selected, parallelized\n\n---\n\n## 10. Edge Cases and Special Handling\n\n### 10.1 Mutation Processing\n- **Lazy Application**: Mutations create entries but don't modify parts immediately\n- **Query Application**: Readers apply mutations on-the-fly from mutation log\n- **Background Application**: Merge task creates new part with mutations applied\n- **Versioning**: Each part knows which mutations it contains\n\n### 10.2 TTL (Time-to-Live)\n- **TTL Index**: Tracks min/max TTL expression value per granule\n- **Cleanup**: Removes expired rows during merges\n- **Group By TTL**: Merge selector can prioritize parts with expired data\n\n### 10.3 Replicated MergeTree\n- **ZooKeeper**: Coordination of merges across replicas\n- **Merge Log**: Entries in ZooKeeper ensure consistent merge ordering\n- **Leader Election**: First replica to claim merge executes it\n- **Data Exchange**: Other replicas can fetch merged part directly\n\n### 10.4 Compact Format Selection\n- **Threshold 1**: `min_bytes_for_wide_part` (default 10MB)\n- **Threshold 2**: `min_rows_for_wide_part` (default 1M rows)\n- **Decision**: Use compact if both size AND row count below thresholds\n- **Conversion**: Automatic during merge if size grows\n\n---\n\n## 11. Key Design Insights\n\n1. **Immutability**: Parts never change once committed, enabling simple concurrency\n2. **Append-Only**: Inserts create new parts, no in-place updates or deletes\n3. **Lazy Merging**: Merges happen asynchronously in background with priority queue\n4. **Sparse Indexing**: Primary key index is ~0.1-1% of data size but can eliminate 90%+ of scans\n5. **Format Flexibility**: Wide format for analytical queries, compact format for write efficiency\n6. **Projection Materialization**: Pre-compute alternative indices automatically\n7. **Coroutine Merges**: Merges implemented as suspendable tasks, not blocking threads\n8. **MVCC Visibility**: Transactions see consistent part set snapshot independent of concurrent changes\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe MergeTree storage engine combines several key innovations:\n- **Columnar + Sorted**: Column-oriented storage with sorted primary key enables both compression and efficient range queries\n- **Hierarchical Merging**: Background merges consolidate small parts into larger ones, balancing write latency and merge cost\n- **Sparse + Layered Indexing**: Multi-level indices (primary key + skip indices) prune data efficiently\n- **Immutable Architecture**: Append-only design eliminates locking complexity and enables simple MVCC\n\nThis architecture makes ClickHouse exceptionally fast for analytical workloads with high insert throughput and complex ad-hoc queries over billions of rows.\n",

    "content": "# ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine Architecture Analysis\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nMergeTree is the core table engine in ClickHouse, designed for highly efficient storage and querying of large volumes of structured data. It uses an append-only design where new data is written as immutable sorted parts, with background merge processes combining parts over time. The architecture is optimized for analytics workloads with column-oriented storage, sophisticated indexing, and intelligent query optimization.\n\n---\n\n## 1. High-Level Architecture # ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine Architecture Analysis

## Executive Summary

MergeTree is the core table engine in ClickHouse, designed for highly efficient storage and querying of large volumes of structured data. It uses an append-only design where new data is written as immutable sorted parts, with background merge processes combining parts over time. The architecture is optimized for analytics workloads with column-oriented storage, sophisticated indexing, and intelligent query optimization.

---

## 1. High-Level Architecture Diagram

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     ClickHouse MergeTree                        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

┌─────────────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐  ┌──────────────────────┐
│   INSERT Path   │  │    MERGE Path    │  │     SELECT Path      │
│                 │  │                  │  │                      │
│ ┌─────────────┐ │  │ ┌──────────────┐ │  │ ┌──────────────────┐ │
│ │  Parser &   │ │  │ │  Merge       │ │  │ │ Query Planner    │ │
│ │  Optimizer  │ │  │ │  Selector    │ │  │ │ & Optimizer      │ │
│ └──────┬──────┘ │  │ └──────┬───────┘ │  │ └────────┬─────────┘ │
│        │        │  │        │         │  │         │           │
│ ┌──────▼──────┐ │  │ ┌──────▼──────┐ │  │ ┌───────▼──────────┐ │
│ │  Data       │ │  │ │  Merge      │ │  │ │ Partition &      │ │
│ │  Writer    │ │  │ │  Algorithm  │ │  │ │ Mark Pruning     │ │
│ └──────┬──────┘ │  │ └──────┬──────┘ │  │ └────────┬─────────┘ │
│        │        │  │        │        │  │         │           │
└────────┼────────┘  └────────┼────────┘  └─────────┼───────────┘
         │                    │                     │
         │                    │            
... (truncated)
